# CSS-Library

> A curated, organized library of **1,958 technically-oriented papers, books, and references** spanning the breadth of computer science.

![files](https://img.shields.io/badge/files-1958-blue) ![categories](https://img.shields.io/badge/categories-20-green) ![PDFs](https://img.shields.io/badge/PDFs-1819-red)

Originally a flat dump of PDFs, now sorted into 20 thematic categories so you can actually find what you're looking for. Topics range from CPU manuals and OS kernels to deep-learning papers, compilers, databases, GPU programming, and reverse engineering.

All content copyright the respective author(s). I make a concerted effort to not publish anything here if the copyright does not permit it. If you spot something that shouldn't be here, please open an issue or PR.

---

## Table of Contents

| # | Category | Count | Topics |
|---|---|---:|---|
| 1 | [Algorithms and Data Structures](#algorithms-and-data-structures) | 254 | Sorting, hashing (perfect/minimal/cuckoo/locality-sensitive), tries and suffix structures, graphs, succinct/probabilistic data structures, search, and complexity-theoretic foundations. |
| 2 | [Compilers and Programming Languages](#compilers-and-programming-languages) | 151 | Compiler construction, JITs, parsers, type systems, formal verification, SAT/SMT, language references (C, C++, Python, R, Rust, Haskell, Go, ...), and PL theory. |
| 3 | [Computer Architecture](#computer-architecture) | 172 | Intel/AMD/ARM/SPARC manuals, microarchitecture, instruction sets (x86, x86-64, AVX/SSE/MMX), caches, TLBs, branch predictors, NVDIMM, PCIe, and BIOS/ACPI. |
| 4 | [Concurrency and Parallelism](#concurrency-and-parallelism) | 193 | Lock-free / wait-free algorithms, transactional memory, RCU, atomics, memory consistency, vectorization, SIMD programming, threading, futexes, and parallel runtimes. |
| 5 | [Operating Systems](#operating-systems) | 111 | Kernels and OS internals across Linux, the BSDs, Solaris, macOS/Mach, BeOS, Plan 9, ReactOS, xv6, and the Mach/UNIX heritage. Includes scheduling, virtual memory, drivers, and system calls. |
| 6 | [Windows Internals](#windows-internals) | 28 | NT kernel internals, WinDbg, ETW, IO completion ports, ALPC, kernel pool, drivers (KMDF/WDF), and MSDN-era deep dives. Includes Microsoft engineering culture pieces. |
| 7 | [Memory Management](#memory-management) | 24 | Allocators (malloc, jemalloc, Hoard, slab/vmem), garbage collection, persistent memory programming, prefetching, and reference counting. |
| 8 | [Storage and File Systems](#storage-and-file-systems) | 28 | NTFS, ZFS, APFS, BeFS, NVMe, io_uring, Fibre Channel, persistent storage, durability, and storage-system case studies. |
| 9 | [Networking](#networking) | 68 | TCP/HTTP/SPDY, BGP, RDMA, DPDK, 10G+ Ethernet, network-stack scaling, IO acceleration, and event-driven server architectures. |
| 10 | [Distributed Systems](#distributed-systems) | 35 | Replication, consensus (Paxos/Raft), CRDTs, distributed tracing (Dapper, Canopy), warehouse-scale systems, and large-scale data processing. |
| 11 | [Databases](#databases) | 203 | Relational and column-stores, B+/Bw/Fractal trees, query processing and optimization, OLAP/OLTP, indexing (bitmap, inverted), Oracle, and DB internals. |
| 12 | [GPU and Graphics](#gpu-and-graphics) | 218 | CUDA programming, NVIDIA/AMD GPU architectures, OpenGL/OpenCL/HIP, ray tracing, the graphics pipeline, GPU sorting/hashing, and visualization. |
| 13 | [AI and Machine Learning](#ai-and-machine-learning) | 173 | Neural networks, deep learning, LLMs (GPT/LLaMA/DeepSeek), transformers, attention mechanisms, RL, embeddings, and classical ML. |
| 14 | [Cryptography and Security](#cryptography-and-security) | 73 | AES/SHA/Keccak, side-channel attacks (Spectre, Meltdown, Flush+Reload), exploitation, ASLR, CFG, security engineering, and forensics. |
| 15 | [Reverse Engineering and Binary Analysis](#reverse-engineering-and-binary-analysis) | 54 | Disassembly, IDA / Hex-Rays, PE/ELF formats, anti-debugging, symbolic execution, dynamic instrumentation (Pin/DynamoRIO), and assembly references. |
| 16 | [Performance and Optimization](#performance-and-optimization) | 38 | Profiling, tracing, latency analysis, microbenchmarking, optimization guides, and high-performance computing techniques. |
| 17 | [Compression and Information Theory](#compression-and-information-theory) | 25 | Huffman, arithmetic, Burrows-Wheeler, integer/unary/Golomb coding, Shannon-era foundations, and bitmap/index compression. |
| 18 | [Mathematics and Statistics](#mathematics-and-statistics) | 39 | Calculus, linear algebra, probability, statistics, discrete math, graph theory, optimization, and biographical/historical pieces. |
| 19 | [Software Engineering and Tools](#software-engineering-and-tools) | 58 | Cheat sheets, style guides, version control, editors (Vim, Emacs), LaTeX/Doxygen/Pandoc, code-review research, and SE essays. |
| 20 | [Misc](#misc) | 13 | Truly miscellaneous: essays, demoscene productions, business/finance specs, aviation, and a handful of items that resist neat categorization. |

**Total: 1,958 files**

### Algorithms and Data Structures

Sorting, hashing (perfect/minimal/cuckoo/locality-sensitive), tries and suffix structures, graphs, succinct/probabilistic data structures, search, and complexity-theoretic foundations.

---

## How the categorization works

Files are sorted by `organize.ps1`, which runs through a priority-ordered list of regex rules (first match wins). The script is **idempotent** -- you can drop new PDFs into the repository root and re-run it; existing categorized files are not touched.

```powershell
# Preview what would happen, with bucket counts:
.\organize.ps1 -DryRun

# Show the full category listing in the dry-run:
.\organize.ps1 -DryRun -ShowAll

# Trace which rule matches a particular filename:
.\organize.ps1 -Trace "FlashAttention-3 - Fast and Accurate Attention.pdf"

# Run for real:
.\organize.ps1
```

## Notes

- Files appear in exactly one category -- the highest-priority match wins, so e.g. *"GPU Hash Tables"* lands in **GPU and Graphics** rather than **Algorithms and Data Structures**.
- A handful of HTML-style pages keep their `_files` sidecar asset folders alongside them.
- The **Misc** bucket is intentionally narrow: only items that genuinely don't fit elsewhere (essays, finance specs, an aviation handbook, etc.) end up there.
